  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e38c217f-69e3-4d74-bac1-d6b9e2770124'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer1136134004277319558">A girl with a secret and a prince on a mission<br/><br/>When Prince Anthony spies Eleanoria Woodston outside her family home dressed as a servant, he knows something is amiss.   <span id="freeText1136134004277319558" style="display:none">A girl with a secret and a prince on a mission<br /><br />When Prince Anthony spies Eleanoria Woodston outside her family home dressed as a servant, he knows something is amiss. Pretending to be John, his cousin’s outrider, he decides to take matters into his own hands and figure out why Ella hasn’t been seen at court. And more importantly why the daughter of one of the wealthiest families in the kingdom dresses like a pauper.<br /><br />Ella has had her own bout of trials, including losing her beloved father and facing the wrath and jealousy of her stepmother and stepsisters. Becoming a servant doesn’t seem all that bad until the handsome John comes into her life, now he appears to be upsetting everything. Never before has she been so unsettled. Just his presence is making her dream of a life beyond this one.<br /><br />When John invites Ella to the ball and she grudgingly accepts, he wonders if he’s truly losing his mind. How would he ever pull off pretending to be John while obviously hosting the ball as Anthony? Especially when the stubborn girl has made it quite obvious she would never attend a ball with a snobbish prince.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227104951?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stef" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stef" href="/user/show/10950473-stef">Stef</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10950473-stef?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10950473-stef?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10950473-stef?shelf=short-stories-novellas">short-stories-novellas</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227104951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7611154136645727654">I was going through the stories in Wattpad when I found this. It was perfect! Well, perfect enough to fill my need of cute lovey-dovey romance stuff. Yes it was a bit cliché, cheesy and not the best out there, but for me, nonetheless, it was nice to find something so simple and short yet creative and did not once made me want to stop reading it. Which is something you rarely find in Wattpad. I say good job to the author and I hope it gets more reads!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2282513151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282513151" />
    <a title="Linnae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/806026-linnae"><img alt="Linnae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222882819p2/806026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2282513151?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linnae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linnae" href="/user/show/806026-linnae">Linnae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=fairy-tales-retold">fairy-tales-retold</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=clean-reads">clean-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/806026-linnae?shelf=cinderella">cinderella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282513151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17930365082104631060">Friendship becomes romance.<br/><br/><br/>Eleanoria Woodston mostly tries not to think about how her life has changed since her beloved father died. Her stepmother, Lady Dashlund, rules the home with an iron hand, with Ella receiving the brunt of it. She now lives in the attic, instead of her own bedroom, and she does all the chores. Her stepsisters get to wear all the finery and are the recipients of Ella's hard work. Even her beloved horse, Sunshine, was sold to help pay the debts.<br/><br/>Prince Anthony has been rop</span>
  <span id="freeText17930365082104631060" style="display:none">Friendship becomes romance.<br /><br /><br />Eleanoria Woodston mostly tries not to think about how her life has changed since her beloved father died. Her stepmother, Lady Dashlund, rules the home with an iron hand, with Ella receiving the brunt of it. She now lives in the attic, instead of her own bedroom, and she does all the chores. Her stepsisters get to wear all the finery and are the recipients of Ella's hard work. Even her beloved horse, Sunshine, was sold to help pay the debts.<br /><br />Prince Anthony has been roped into paying a formal visit to the Dashlund household, along with his friend Lord Gavenston. On the way there, he spots a woman on the grounds, whom he is certain is Eleanoria--a friend and rival from his childhood, when he used to sneak out of the castle and enter into local horse races. It can't be her, though. She's is dressed as a servant; she, whose father was one of the wealthiest merchants in the kingdom. Prince Anthony decides he must find out what is going on, so he once again dons the old ruse and nickname "John" and leaves Lord Gavenston to make his way on his own with the Dashlund sisters.<br /><br />* * * * *<br />This version stayed fairly close to the original. What I liked about it, though, was that Ella and the Prince renewed their friendship long before the ball. The Prince got a lot more backstory, which was nice. He was more than a cardboard cutout. In this one, the King was dying, and he had the weight of that on his shoulders. <br /><br />That being said, there was a part that tended toward insta-love. It had been 3 days (I think) since Ella and Anthony had renewed their acquaintance, and she started going on about all that she loved about him, naming each facial feature in turn (yes, it was awkward even reading about it.) Then at the end, she said something about how she didn't want him to take it wrong, because she knew they were just friends. Um...what?  Maybe that was just evidence of her own confusion. Anyway, they continued to meet for several more months before really declaring undying devotion to one another.<br /><br /><br />Content: Clean.<br /><br />I blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ofbooksandblooms.com">www.ofbooksandblooms.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17930365082104631060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3397039363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_670484690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670484690" />
    <a title="Ally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10598644-ally"><img alt="Ally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427068181p2/10598644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670484690?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ally" href="/user/show/10598644-ally">Ally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670484690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer22295439793390678">Wow! I love this retelling of Cinderella better than any other. (Except for Cinder (Cinder #1) by Marissa Meyer) (Read that book if you don't know what I'm talking about). Cinderella (and Cinder) are absolutely delightful. Cinderella is recommended to readers who are at least eleven years old.<br/><br/>The plot isn't twisty or anything, but everything is pretty well written and fitted together. Every word flows and nothing is too wrong or anything. I like the conflict of the story, but it isn't too big of</span>
  <span id="freeText22295439793390678" style="display:none">Wow! I love this retelling of Cinderella better than any other. (Except for Cinder (Cinder #1) by Marissa Meyer) (Read that book if you don't know what I'm talking about). Cinderella (and Cinder) are absolutely delightful. Cinderella is recommended to readers who are at least eleven years old.<br /><br />The plot isn't twisty or anything, but everything is pretty well written and fitted together. Every word flows and nothing is too wrong or anything. I like the conflict of the story, but it isn't too big of a deal, especially because I know what will happen in the end. We always do know what happens in fairy tale retellings. Usually.<br /><br />The ending is so "Happily Ever After." It's a nice change after reading bloody endings and cliffhangers. I'm so sick of them and authors who love, just love, to torture readers like you and me. There should be a law that states "All books must and always not have cliffhangers or loose endings."<br /><br />I like how the author uses switching POVs to tell the Cinderella story. From the hilarious Prince to the 'stubborn' girl, we see the world of Cinderella. I wish, simply wish, for a POV from one of the stepsisters. Or maybe not. I wouldn't want to listen to the rantings and selfish thoughts of the evil stepsister. <br /><br />Characters:<br /><br />Eleanoria Woodston, or what we and the prince call her, Ella, is a wonderful character. She's a little too ignorant and thick for my liking, but is still above the range of my hatred. The only reason I like is because this girl has guts to stand up. After all that abuse, insults, she rises against her bullies (stepmother and stepsister). Which is what every bullied kid or person should do.<br /><br />Prince Anthony is so dashing. I can't help but fall in love in his character and sweet charming words. His little reactions to the hilarious pushings and tauntings of his mother are funny and innocent. He likes Eleanoria, but won't admit it to his mother, no matter what his mother says or do. (We have to love the mother). <br /><br />Rating: Three out of Five<br /><br />-ofpaperandwords.blogspot.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="22295439793390678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_863820730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863820730" />
    <a title="Silverin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6983087-silverin"><img alt="Silverin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408839621p2/6983087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863820730?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silverin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silverin" href="/user/show/6983087-silverin">Silverin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6983087-silverin?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6983087-silverin?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6983087-silverin?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6983087-silverin?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6983087-silverin?shelf=cinderella">cinderella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863820730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2617386921308868182">First Line: <blockquote> <i>"Ella picked up the last basket of clothing, her arms strained from attempting to carry the heavy, wet mass the twelve or so feet to the drying line."</i> </blockquote><br/><p>This is a very non-magical fairytale retelling of Cinderella. All the aspects that made the original story wonderful for me are missing here. There is no fairy godmother, no magical transformation, no running away at midnight and leaving behind a glass slipper, and no sense of awe or wonder at the discovery of the identity of the myst</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2617386921308868182" style="display:none">First Line: <blockquote> <i>"Ella picked up the last basket of clothing, her arms strained from attempting to carry the heavy, wet mass the twelve or so feet to the drying line."</i> </blockquote><br /><p>This is a very non-magical fairytale retelling of Cinderella. All the aspects that made the original story wonderful for me are missing here. There is no fairy godmother, no magical transformation, no running away at midnight and leaving behind a glass slipper, and no sense of awe or wonder at the discovery of the identity of the mysterious and beautiful maiden at the ball since everybody already knows her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Also the fact that a ball was held so soon - just 2 months- after the King's death seems inappropriate. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There are also several typos and errors that should have been edited out such as "He ran his fingers through his hair and rested his knees upon his elbows," or "Her faint worries were for not," or Ella asking "Anthony, were in the world are we?"</p><br /><p>What I did like - the only thing I actually like - in this particular retelling is the character of Prince Anthony/John. So often in fairy tales we have just the princesses' POV, but if there is one thing I really appreciate in Jenni James' stories is that the princes are given just as much attention and a personality as the princesses. I have also read James' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17673256.The_Frog_Prince__Faerie_Tale_Collection___8_" title="The Frog Prince (Faerie Tale Collection, #8) by Jenni James" rel="nofollow noopener">The Frog Prince</a> and found it a better retelling than the original, which I've never really liked, due to the inclusion of a very 'charming' prince. And for that I'm going to try a few other of her books in this collection.</p><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2617386921308868182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer627189094" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10131497900124864830">I see a lot of people have really enjoyed this book, but I did not find it very well written at all. A new character arrives 2/3 of the way through, just to provide the answer to all Ella's problems. There is no explanation as to why he waited this long to give her the answers he had, and we never hear from him again. And Ella and the Prince kiss each other a whole lot and then still apparently aren't sure of their feelings for each other!? One of the step sisters all of a sudden becomes nice, a</span>
  <span id="freeText10131497900124864830" style="display:none">I see a lot of people have really enjoyed this book, but I did not find it very well written at all. A new character arrives 2/3 of the way through, just to provide the answer to all Ella's problems. There is no explanation as to why he waited this long to give her the answers he had, and we never hear from him again. And Ella and the Prince kiss each other a whole lot and then still apparently aren't sure of their feelings for each other!? One of the step sisters all of a sudden becomes nice, and there is no explanation as to why. Also, I expected the step mother to be more of an adversary. We were constantly told how angry and afraid she was of Ella going to the ball, but when the time came, she just let her go, and apparently got over whatever was bothering her, because the story just plodded along to the ending without any attempt by the antagonist to stop it. As a Cinderella retelling, some of the ideas Jenni James had were unique and interesting, but it was not executed or fleshed out well enough for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10131497900124864830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2228529128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2228529128" />
    <a title="Elentarien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1529438-elentarien"><img alt="Elentarien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561491966p2/1529438.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2228529128?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elentarien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elentarien" href="/user/show/1529438-elentarien">Elentarien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1529438-elentarien?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1529438-elentarien?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228529128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13400020113809133177">I found this to be a very simple retelling of the fairy tale. All in all, I enjoyed it, though I found it to be. . .underdeveloped. The editing was rough and in several places caused reading to cease and backtracking to occur to figure out what had just been read.<br/><br/>Very little actually *happened*, the villian/s were barely present, and when things started coming to a head. . .nothing actually happened. They did not truly *do* anything. <br/><br/>I did appreciate that Ella and the prince knew each other befo</span>
  <span id="freeText13400020113809133177" style="display:none">I found this to be a very simple retelling of the fairy tale. All in all, I enjoyed it, though I found it to be. . .underdeveloped. The editing was rough and in several places caused reading to cease and backtracking to occur to figure out what had just been read.<br /><br />Very little actually *happened*, the villian/s were barely present, and when things started coming to a head. . .nothing actually happened. They did not truly *do* anything. <br /><br />I did appreciate that Ella and the prince knew each other before the ball, but it was fairly clear they never really "knew" each other as children. . .just as competitors, but not as friends. As adults, this leads to a bad case of 'insta-love' with no real development on friendship or actually knowing each other. While they definitely spend more time with each other than 'just' at the ball (thank you!) the love story is a *bit* more believable. I would have liked to see more depth to the relationship. Near the end emotions were still flip-flopping around. There was not much sense of the relationship really growing in a believable manner. The prince also came across as a bit too 'perfect'. With the perfect life, perfect parents, perfect situation (apart from his father dying) and no real character developing areas. <br /><br />There was, I noted, and appreciated, some effort to show the mental trauma Ella lived under. The abuse she endured and the mental state she lived with, doubting her own worth, etc. While only the tip of the iceberg for someone living in an abusive situation, it was nice to see she was not 'perfectly fine' after all that time.<br /><br />All in all, a light read to be enjoyed in an evening, but not much depth to this story. Like the other three of this series I have read, it had an interesting concept, and seemed the nice framework for a deeper story, but was not fully developed and realized.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13400020113809133177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3234597468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3234597468" />
    <a title="Leia Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38076785-leia-rose"><img alt="Leia Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542636458p2/38076785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3234597468?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leia Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leia Rose" href="/user/show/38076785-leia-rose">Leia Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38076785-leia-rose?shelf=non-magical-fantasy">non-magical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3234597468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13204586921248314690">I like the notion of Cinderella and her prince meeting each other prior to the ball so there's no "fell in love after one night of dancing" thing. But having them meet in advance is rendered completely pointless (in terms of romance) if they fall in love immediately!!<br/><br/>Ella and John used to race each other as children. It's not made clear where these races all of the kids had were held or how this was "a thing" for what I assume is middle class children(they have to be rich enough to own horses bu</span>
  <span id="freeText13204586921248314690" style="display:none">I like the notion of Cinderella and her prince meeting each other prior to the ball so there's no "fell in love after one night of dancing" thing. But having them meet in advance is rendered completely pointless (in terms of romance) if they fall in love immediately!!<br /><br />Ella and John used to race each other as children. It's not made clear where these races all of the kids had were held or how this was "a thing" for what I assume is middle class children(they have to be rich enough to own horses but weren't necessarily nobility). But Ella use to win all the time with John in second apparently. That was their entire "we used to know each other" history. Ella's been gone for years and clearly the two haven't thought anything about the other.<br /><br />But one day John sees her and is like hey that's so and so! Why's she dressed like a servant? Has a short chat with her. Comes by the next day and they spend some time together. Then on their third encounter as adults they start off their meeting with kissing. So after one brief conversation, and a few hours the next day together they're now in love.<br /><br />Oh, but John had just said earlier how he wouldn't fall easy. *eye roll*<br /><br />So that's our romance. John knows who Ella is the whole time and invites her to the ball and even picks her up. There goes the mystery girl at the ball and the leaving at midnight because of magic and a glass slipper, etc. No magic at all in this story or hunting to find the mystery girl. There's also no pressure for the prince to pick a bride at this event and it isn't expected that he will. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I actually think he is the king by that point. At the very least his father is dead and he's about to become king so no one to order a bride must be chosen.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One of the stepsister's suddenly has a change of heart and becomes super nice to Ella. Once Ella gets an official invitation to the ball from the queen the stepmother backs off. She has one of her daughter's give Ella a dress, offers to have Ella ride with them at the ball, and is basically unseen for the rest of the book. She's not a problem at home or at the ball. It makes her very lackluster as a villain. The other stepsister is similar with no big confrontation and only her making a tiny shriek at the ball when Ella shows up.<br /><br />I would've quit at about 50% but since the story is short I figured I might as well trudge on. Instalove, no suspense, missing some key cinderella plot points, and a meh antagonist were enough to make this a bleh read for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13204586921248314690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2136632784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136632784" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22152499-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373670310p2/22152499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136632784?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/22152499-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2136632784&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136632784" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4953868029181987405">Somehow there was absolutely no conflict in the book. Ella was just a girl who let everyone walk all over her and had low self esteem. The Prince was a pampered boy who got everything he wanted and his parents were perfect. The Prince mentions at the beginning that he didn't want to marry someone he didn't know and would not fall in love easily, but they somehow contradicts himself on what seems like the next page when he falls for Ella after seeing her just once. They say they have "been friend</span>
  <span id="freeText4953868029181987405" style="display:none">Somehow there was absolutely no conflict in the book. Ella was just a girl who let everyone walk all over her and had low self esteem. The Prince was a pampered boy who got everything he wanted and his parents were perfect. The Prince mentions at the beginning that he didn't want to marry someone he didn't know and would not fall in love easily, but they somehow contradicts himself on what seems like the next page when he falls for Ella after seeing her just once. They say they have "been friends since childhood", but really they only "knew" each other because they raced horses against each other once; that is not actually knowing someone. There is no fairy godmother and no real glass slippers, I'm not even sure besides her name and that she has a stepmother why this is a Cinderella story? It reads like a Hallmark movie that is so cheesy and ridiculous that at times it was hard to get through without taking a break for laughing and heavy eye rolling. I don't think I would read this again, and I would only recommend this book to those who are in for a quick read and low expectations on character development and plot. </span>

<div id="review_3351734750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3351734750" />
    <a title="Iamshee Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58068939-iamshee-reads"><img alt="Iamshee Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599788662p2/58068939.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13747451334433045933">Finished reading this last April.. Kinda bored with QUARANTINE and all so I decided to pick this book and read...<br/><br/>I am fan of Cinderella stories, may it be a book or movie version, I read and watch it.   <span id="freeText13747451334433045933" style="display:none">Finished reading this last April.. Kinda bored with QUARANTINE and all so I decided to pick this book and read...<br /><br />I am fan of Cinderella stories, may it be a book or movie version, I read and watch it. This book is a re-tell of a fairytale by Jenni James. I find it nice but there is something missing on the book because I feel the story was being rushed. I don't know but it feels like it.<br /><br />The love story between Eleanora and Prince Anthony is good, however, I think the writer forgot the stepmother, Lady Dashlund. I was hoping to see more of her being a wicked stepmom to Eleanora. I mean more scenes and interactions that will depict her cruelty to the heroine. They just gone missing to the story as the chapters went on.<br /><br />This book has a lot of potential tho, only if Miss Jenni gave it a proper attention. Cinderella story is a classic fairytale known to most of us, loved by most of us especially girls.<br /><br />Still this book is a nice read. I could recommend it to those who wants light reading.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17713773475016962030">The Daddy Issues in this book were too real.... Got me in the feels big time!   <span id="freeText17713773475016962030" style="display:none">The Daddy Issues in this book were too real.... Got me in the feels big time! But it was a cute read, and I enjoyed it.<br /><br />Although this doesn't seem like a very different retelling... There was no Fairy-Godmother, and no 'When the clock strikes 12...' business. <br /><br />There are so many different re-tellings of this story. The one where she goes to the ball wearing her step-sister's stuff, and they shred the clothes off her and scratch her face bloody....<br />And the other version where she loses the slipper and when the Prince gets to her door to make the girls try it on her stepsisters cut off their big toes in hopes of the shoe fitting.... it still didn't and during the Prince and Cinderella's happily ever after they made the sisters dance on hot coals... possibly while black birds plucked out their eyes.... not sure - BUT TRUE STORY!<br /><br />A good read, definitely cute, and a good love story. I'm just not so sure about the retelling part. It seems basically the same to me.<br /><br />~Simone</span>

But Anthony redeemed himself and I thought their relationship was so cute. I loved that they had met before and it wasn't just </span>
  <span id="freeText3787587851230200626" style="display:none">This was a cute story and a fun retelling of Cinderella. Okay so at first I didn't love Anthony. I thought he was a bit arrogant and seemed like he was just talking with Ella to help her so he could feel good about himself. Some who read this may wonder where I got that idea but that is how I felt at first. I loved Ella. Some of the supporting characters were great too. But Anthony redeemed himself and I thought their relationship was so cute. I loved that they had met before and it wasn't just an insta love at first sight unbelievable deal. Their interactions were cute and sweet and I quite enjoyed this book. It was a quick but entertaining read. </span>

<div id="review_2213985707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2213985707" />
    <a title="Naisha Khatani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49708618-naisha-khatani"><img alt="Naisha Khatani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513260143p2/49708618.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naisha Khatani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naisha Khatani" href="/user/show/49708618-naisha-khatani">Naisha Khatani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2213985707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4507744103172007832">This was a cute retelling of Cinderella, for lack of a better word. I'm actually not too fond of the original because it shows a helpless girl that falls in love with a prince that doesn't even know her name. I loved how Ella and Anthony's feelings towards each other developed over time rather than in one night. I feel as though the stepmother's character could have been developed a little more and could have been more involved in the story. Over all, very enjoyable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3443109133" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3443109133" />
    <a title="Rachael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70012583-rachael"><img alt="Rachael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501650344p2/70012583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3443109133?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachael" href="/user/show/70012583-rachael">Rachael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/49125494-cinderella">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3443109133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4133210398772815381"><strong>Wonderful twist to the original fairytale </strong><br/><br/>I loved this sweet romance based on the fairytale Cinderella.<br/>Ella is such a wonderful, sweet girl. Although treated horribly after her father’s passing away it does not make her bitter or vengeful. Price Anthony is any girls dream.<br/><br/>I loved the relationship that developed between Ella and Anthony as they grew to love each other. Would recommend for any age.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7HqEpoTwvVRUtt+MgdvSNwXWksuz+ldPvaGGsqWIbhbSl4AJvztvFmnqsDKnE727vbYdaAaA8RqtDsvN7lDiCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cLJqH/XfjJFFKT/DaW2YBJRloaUBZOUtxmM1UI0MaWpOX26wzhRe03h1UH1PpfeILAUuBrQeQ3jWzHgvxtTldA==')})
  }
